### Post by -grubby on 2009-01-01
January 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

[list]
[*] Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

[*] If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

[*] Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

[*] The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

[*] The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

[*] Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

[*] To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.
[/list]

---

### Post by ayoli on 2009-01-01
> **strAlan said:**
> I want this desktop: [[IMG]http://img122.imageshack.us/img122/9746/08092008ic6.th.png[/IMG]](http://img122.imageshack.us/my.php?image=08092008ic6.png) Hopefully Google will lead me to the answer :D

This is one of my september desktops.
infos are in the screenshot ([large view]("http://ayozone.org/wp-content/gallery/screenshots-september-2008/08092008.png"))
The screenlets used here are : pidginscreenlet, widescape weather and circleclock. All are on gnome-look.org
The system info on the bottom right is conky with stylebats and pizzadude bullets from dafont.com
here's the conkyrc file (you may need to adjust the mounts points, network interfaces, ...) :
```

background yes
#background no
use_xft yes
xftfont Myriad pro:normal:size=9

xftalpha 1.0
update_interval 3.0
total_run_times 0
double_buffer yes

own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type normal 		#or : desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#own_window no
#own_window_type normal
#own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

minimum_size 220 5
maximum_width 85 5

draw_shades no ### SHADOW ###
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes

default_outline_color black
default_color white ### Text Color ###
default_shade_color black

alignment bottom_right
gap_x 20
gap_y 0

no_buffers yes
cpu_avg_samples 2

override_utf8_locale yes
#uppercase yes

TEXT
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}a${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${cpu cpu0}%
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}a${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${cpu cpu1}%
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}g${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${memperc}%
   ${exec /home/ayoli/local/bin/bat_state}${if_existing /home/ayoli/.bat_state charged}${font StyleBats:size=18}o${else}${font StyleBats:size=18}p${endif}${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -4}    ${battery_percent C1AB}%
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}i${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${swapperc}%
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}4${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${if_mounted /home}${fs_free  /home}${else}--${endif}
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}x${font}${alignr 2}${voffset -3}    ${if_mounted /media/store}${fs_free  /media/store}${else}--${endif}
   ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}M${font}${alignr 2}    ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}
   ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}S${font}${alignr 2}    ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}

```
Happy new year :)

### Post by AFarris01 on 2009-01-01
My Desktop, with a Christmas-y theme!

Wallpaper: Blue Christmas from DigitalBlasphemy.com (was in free gallerys, no longer there tho :( )

Icon Theme: Dropline Nou (gnome-look.org)

Window Borders: DarkIce Colors (also from gnome-look)

Pointer: Dart3D (gnome-look again)

Conky File:
```
# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background no

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2

out_to_console no

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 7x12
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 7x12
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*
#font -artwiz-snap-normal-r-normal-*-*-100-*-*-p-*-iso8859-1

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
#xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=8
xftfont URW Chancery L:size=8

own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_colour blue
# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

on_bottom yes

# mail spool
# mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1
# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_taskbar
own_window_type override

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 325 5
maximum_width 325

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders no

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color white
default_outline_color white

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 30
gap_y 15

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# Possible variables to be used:
#
#      Variable         Arguments                  Description                
#  acpiacadapter                     ACPI ac adapter state.                   
#  acpifan                           ACPI fan state                           
#  acpitemp                          ACPI temperature.                        
#  adt746xcpu                        CPU temperature from therm_adt746x       
#  adt746xfan                        Fan speed from therm_adt746x             
#  battery           (num)           Remaining capasity in ACPI or APM        
#                                    battery. ACPI battery number can be      
#                                    given as argument (default is BAT0).     
#  buffers                           Amount of memory buffered                
#  cached                            Amount of memory cached                  
#  color             (color)         Change drawing color to color            
#  cpu                               CPU usage in percents                    
#  cpubar            (height)        Bar that shows CPU usage, height is      
#                                    bar's height in pixels                   
#  downspeed         net             Download speed in kilobytes              
#  downspeedf        net             Download speed in kilobytes with one     
#                                    decimal                                  
#  exec              shell command   Executes a shell command and displays    
#                                    the output in torsmo. warning: this      
#                                    takes a lot more resources than other    
#                                    variables. I'd recommend coding wanted   
#                                    behaviour in C and posting a patch :-).  
#  execi             interval, shell Same as exec but with specific interval. 
#                    command         Interval can't be less than              
#                                    update_interval in configuration.        
#  fs_bar            (height), (fs)  Bar that shows how much space is used on 
#                                    a file system. height is the height in   
#                                    pixels. fs is any file on that file      
#                                    system.                                  
#  fs_free           (fs)            Free space on a file system available    
#                                    for users.                               
#  fs_free_perc      (fs)            Free percentage of space on a file       
#                                    system available for users.              
#  fs_size           (fs)            File system size                         
#  fs_used           (fs)            File system used space                   
#  hr                (height)        Horizontal line, height is the height in 
#                                    pixels                                   
#  i2c               (dev), type, n  I2C sensor from sysfs (Linux 2.6). dev   
#                                    may be omitted if you have only one I2C  
#                                    device. type is either in (or vol)       
#                                    meaning voltage, fan meaning fan or temp 
#                                    meaning temperature. n is number of the  
#                                    sensor. See /sys/bus/i2c/devices/ on     
#                                    your local computer.                     
#  kernel                            Kernel version                           
#  loadavg           (1), (2), (3)   System load average, 1 is for past 1     
#                                    minute, 2 for past 5 minutes and 3 for   
#                                    past 15 minutes.                         
#  machine                           Machine, i686 for example                
#  mails                             Mail count in mail spool. You can use    
#                                    program like fetchmail to get mails from 
#                                    some server using your favourite         
#                                    protocol. See also new_mails.            
#  mem                               Amount of memory in use                  
#  membar            (height)        Bar that shows amount of memory in use   
#  memmax                            Total amount of memory                   
#  memperc                           Percentage of memory in use              
#  new_mails                         Unread mail count in mail spool.         
#  nodename                          Hostname                                 
#  outlinecolor      (color)         Change outline color                     
#  pre_exec          shell command   Executes a shell command one time before 
#                                    torsmo displays anything and puts output 
#                                    as text.                                 
#  processes                         Total processes (sleeping and running)   
#  running_processes                 Running processes (not sleeping),        
#                                    requires Linux 2.6                       
#  shadecolor        (color)         Change shading color                     
#  stippled_hr       (space),        Stippled (dashed) horizontal line        
#                    (height)        
#  swapbar           (height)        Bar that shows amount of swap in use     
#  swap                              Amount of swap in use                    
#  swapmax                           Total amount of swap                     
#  swapperc                          Percentage of swap in use                
#  sysname                           System name, Linux for example           
#  time              (format)        Local time, see man strftime to get more 
#                                    information about format                 
#  totaldown         net             Total download, overflows at 4 GB on     
#                                    Linux with 32-bit arch and there doesn't 
#                                    seem to be a way to know how many times  
#                                    it has already done that before torsmo   
#                                    has started.                             
#  totalup           net             Total upload, this one too, may overflow 
#  updates                           Number of updates (for debugging)        
#  upspeed           net             Upload speed in kilobytes                
#  upspeedf          net             Upload speed in kilobytes with one       
#                                    decimal                                  
#  uptime                            Uptime                                   
#  uptime_short                      Uptime in a shorter format               
#
#  seti_prog                         Seti@home current progress
#  seti_progbar      (height)        Seti@home current progress bar
#  seti_credit                       Seti@hoome total user credit


# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument
#${font Dungeon:style=Bold:pixelsize=10}I can change the font as well
#${font Verdana:size=10}as many times as I choose
#${font Perry:size=10}Including UTF-8,
# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen
#${font Grunge:size=12}${time %a  %b  %d}${alignr -25}${time %k:%M}

#${color #932D0D} Public IP $alignr ${color #000000}${execi 14400 wget -O - http://whatismyip.org/ | tail} 


TEXT
${color #8FB5DA}$sysname $kernel $machine - $nodename

${color #8FB5DA}${execi 1000 cat /proc/cpuinfo | grep 'model name' | sed -e 's/model name.*: //'} ${color lightgrey}${freq_dyn}Mhz
${color #8FB5DA}Usage:${color #8FB5DA} ${color lightgrey}${cpu}% ${color #8FB5DA}${cpubar}
${color #8FB5DA}${cpugraph 000000 0077ff}
${color #8FB5DA}Processes:${color lightgrey} $processes  ${color #8FB5DA}Running:${color lightgrey} $running_processes ${color #8FB5DA}CPU0:${color lightgrey} ${execi 5 ~/.conky/sensorsCPUtemp.sh}C${color lightgrey} ${color #8FB5DA}CPU1:${color lightgrey} ${execi 5 ~/.conky/sensorsCPUtemp1.sh}C

${color #8FB5DA}RAM:${color lightgrey} $mem/$memmax - $memperc% ${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${membar 5,110}
${color #8FB5DA}SWAP:${color lightgrey} $swap/$swapmax - $swapperc% ${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${swapbar 5,110}

${color #8FB5DA}Disk Activity:
${color #8FB5DA}${diskiograph 000000 0077ff}

${color #8FB5DA}Hard Disks:
${color #8FB5DA} Root ${color lightgrey}${fs_used /} / ${fs_size /}${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${fs_bar 5,120 /}
${color #8FB5DA} Home ${color lightgrey}${fs_used /home} / ${fs_size /home}${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${fs_bar 5,120 /home}
${color #8FB5DA} WINSYS ${color lightgrey}${fs_used /media/sda1} / ${fs_size /media/sda1}${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${fs_bar 5,120 /media/sda1}
${color #8FB5DA} BIGGIN ${color lightgrey}${fs_used /media/sdb1} / ${fs_size /media/sdb1}${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}${fs_bar 5,120 /media/sdb1}

${color #8FB5DA}CPU Usage         PID     CPU%   MEM% ${alignr}${color #8FB5DA}Mem Usage         PID     CPU%   MEM% 
${color lightgrey} ${top name 1} ${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1} ${top mem 1} ${alignr}${color lightgrey} ${top_mem name 1} ${top_mem pid 1} ${top_mem cpu 1} ${top_mem mem 1}
${color #8FB5DA} ${top name 2} ${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2} ${top mem 2} ${alignr}${color #8FB5DA} ${top_mem name 2} ${top_mem pid 2} ${top_mem cpu 2} ${top_mem mem 2}
${color #8FB5DA} ${top name 3} ${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3} ${top mem 3}${alignr}${color #8FB5DA} ${top_mem name 3} ${top_mem pid 3} ${top_mem cpu 3} ${top_mem mem 3}

$alignc ${color #8FB5DA}Public IP: ${color lightgrey}${execi 5 ~/.conky/fetchIP}
${color #8FB5DA}Hardline: ${color lightgrey}${addr eth0}
${color #8FB5DA}Down:${color lightgrey} ${downspeed eth0} k/s $alignr${color #8FB5DA} Up:${color lightgrey} ${upspeed eth0} k/s
${color #8FB5DA}${downspeedgraph eth0 12,120 000000 0077ff 180} $alignr${color #8FB5DA}${upspeedgraph eth0 12,120 000000 0077ff 25}
${color lightgrey}${totaldown eth0}           $alignr${color lightgrey}${totalup eth0}

${color #8FB5DA}Wireless: ${color lightgrey}${addr wlan0}
${color #8FB5DA}Down:${color lightgrey} ${downspeed wlan0} k/s $alignr${color #8FB5DA} Up:${color lightgrey} ${upspeed wlan0} k/s
${color #8FB5DA}${downspeedgraph wlan0 12,120 000000 0077ff 180} $alignr${color #8FB5DA}${upspeedgraph wlan0 12,120 000000 0077ff 25}
${color lightgrey}${totaldown wlan0}           $alignr${color lightgrey}${totalup wlan0}


```

Are you sure the most recent version doesn't produce the same effect on your side? Currently, somewhere on the top of the gtkrc file, the theme states: 

```

        GtkMenuBar::shadow_type = GTK_SHADOW_NONE
        #GtkToolbar::shadow_type = GTK_SHADOW_NONE
```

If you enable the second line again, it will produce a completely flat look, both on the toolbar and on the menubar. Or it should.

/home/daffy $ cat .gtkrc-2.0 
# DO NOT EDIT!  This file will be overwritten by LXAppearance.
# Any customization should be done in ~/.gtkrc-2.0.mine

gtk-theme-name="Milk-2.1g"
gtk-icon-theme-name="black-white_2-Style"
gtk-font-name="Verdana 10"
gtk-toolbar-style=2
include "/home/daffy/.gtkrc-2.0.mine"

### Post by Sprut1 on 2009-01-02

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-01-02
> **Islington said:**
> also the other thing that I noticed that the panel is defaulted to 29 pix. this is way too big on smaller laptop screen. where is this defined in the gtkrc?

It is not defaulted to 29 pixels, but the fact that: 

```
style "panel" {
	xthickness = 3
	ythickness = 3
```

...on lines 325-327 of the gtkrc file seems to create huge borders around the buttons. This is another issue I wasn't noticing because I'm using a custom background for the panels on GNOME, and that makes the panels look slimmer. That said, if you reduce those thickness values to 1, it should be enough.

---

### Post by BIGtrouble77 on 2009-01-03
[[IMG]http://img167.imageshack.us/img167/4861/screenshotdi8.th.png[/IMG]](http://img167.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshotdi8.png)
This is a shot from my netbook.

Gnome with no bottom panel or dock.  It's purely [alt] [tab] and custom key driven.

Emerald Theme- I customized the old beryl theme and added some features.
gtk2 theme- Gnome colors.  By far my favorite theme.  It looks perfect and rivals osx in polish.

icon theme- gnome colors wise.  I have the red gnome colors icon set for root so I can easily see when I'm in root mode.

using un-antialiased msttcore fonts.  I used the base rules from sharpfonts.com and added a few extra for other fonts.  

compiz fusion is enabled with some custom effects and many custom key bindings.

---

### Post by e_torano on 2009-01-03
**Theme:** [Shiki-Colors (Brave)](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Shiki-Colors?content=86717)
**Icons:** [GNOME-Brave](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Shiki-Colors?content=86717)

If you want the theme and icons together without downloading more than one, the maker has a script you can download that installs everything. It's at the bottom of the gnome-look page linked to above.

**Emerald Theme:** [Scaled Black Mod](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Scaled+Black+Mod?content=45402)
**Wallpaper:** [Made By Me](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu+-+Breaking+Free?content=94943)
**Conky.rc:** 

```
# .conkyrc by fabsh <fabsh@lamerk.org>
# Based on ideas and code from the CunchBang Linux forums at http://crunchbanglinux.org
# v. 1.0

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont DejaVu Sans:size=8
xftalpha 0.8
text_buffer_size 2048

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

own_window no
own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_type override
own_window_type desktop
#own_window_type normal #use this if you want a nice shadow to appear around conky

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 180 0
#maximum_width 200

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 0

# border margins
border_margin 5

# border width
border_width 0

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
#default_shade_color black
#default_outline_color grey
own_window_colour grey

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 12
gap_y 12

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase yes

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

TEXT


${font Radio Space:size=30}${color5}EUAN
${voffset -20}${color1}$hr
${voffset -20}${font Radio Space:size=14}${color1}${time %A %d %Y}
${font Radio Space:size=55}${color1}${time %H:%M}
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}CPU: ${font Verana:size=8}${cpubar cpu1 10,150} ${cpu cpu1}%
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}RAM: ${font Verdana:size=8}${mem} / ${memmax} (${memperc}%)
$hr
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}IP Address: ${font Verana:size=8}${gw_ip}
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}Total Download: ${font Verana:size=8}${totaldown wlan0}
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}Total Upload: ${font Verana:size=8}${totalup wlan0}
${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}Up Speed: ${font Verdana:size=8}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${font Verana:style=Bold:size=9}Down Speed: ${font Verdana:size=8}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s
```

[B]
Screenshot:[/B]

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-01-03
Just wanted to say I updated CianoSmooth (check my drop.io), and it seems the bugs are gone. I am keeping the toolbar gradient, but this time the theme should not present any odd lines between the toolbar itself and the menubar. Also, as you can see, the panel's size is reasonable even when there is no panel background applied. From what I think I learnt, writing a specific x/ythickness for the panel style is problematic by itself, so I just removed those lines altogether.

[[IMG]http://e.imagehost.org/t/0867/ecra2.jpg[/IMG]](http://e.imagehost.org/view/0867/ecra2)

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2009-01-04
> **ddnev45 said:**
> E17, switched over to the cerium theme; more stable than some past installs. Got it looking the way I want, just a couple things to fix/learn.

Looks like you need to use gtk-theme-switch or gtk-chtheme or (my favorite) lxappearance, to configure your GTK theme.  Unless, that is, you just like the default one.  For that matter, you could just manually configure your ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file.  It's pretty straightforward.

Example: ```
gtk-theme-name="Aurora"
gtk-icon-theme-name="Eikon"
gtk-font-name="Verdana 10"
gtk-toolbar-style=2
```

### Post by grotto on 2009-01-05
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Very funky.

Question about KDE4.x: where can I find details of requirements for running the accelerated compositing?

I remember when I tried 4.1, as well as being extremely crash-happy, it wouldn't give me accelerated compositing, instead falling back to the un-accelerated xorg composite extension.

I'm running the open source ATi drivers for my Radeon 9550. Have direct rendering and texture_from_pixmap (though apparently not in a, "direct rendering context", so compiz falls back to indirect rendering).

Kwin's composition effects under KDE 4.1 didn't work well for me, either. I'm currently using the 4.2 beta and it has greatly improved.

I'm using an r300-based ATI card and the open-source drivers, as well. So I'd assume you meet the requirements. 

You might find [this how-to]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RadeonDriver") or [this one]("http://websvn.kde.org/*checkout*/trunk/KDE/kdebase/workspace/kwin/COMPOSITE_HOWTO") helpful. According [to this]("http://techbase.kde.org/Projects/KWin/HW#ATI_Radeon_9550_.28r350.29"), [the Radeon 9550] works with XRender and TFP. Doesn't work with SHM. I have no idea what "SHM" is. There is a [GPU-Performance guide]("http://userbase.kde.org/GPU-Performance"), but it mainly covers nVidia currently. 

I had to tweak xorg.conf a bit to get composition effects working smoothly. Enabling EXA from XAA helped quite noticeably.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-01-05
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I love it!  How did you manage a stripe-free progressbar?  Is that a new feature?  And there's a new SVN out?!?  Is there a list of the new features?  Am I asking too many questions?  :P


Yep, Cimi started developping Murrine again!!! :D And there have been almost daily revisions, too.
There is now a new option to change the style of the progressbars. It's the progressbarstyle:

```
progressbarstyle    0 = nothing, 1 = striped, 2 = cells
```

As for the list of the new features, I have no idea where to find it. Perhaps I'm just too lazy. What I usually do is to observe others' themes and then try my luck.

---

```
progressbarstyle    0 = nothing, 1 = striped, 2 = cells
```

As for the list of the new features, I have no idea where to find it. Perhaps I'm just too lazy. What I usually do is to observe others' themes and then try my luck.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-01-05
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Where did you find the new Murrine SVN?

Well, in the same place as usual. I basically pull a SVN snapshot and compile it. 

```
svn checkout http://svn.gnome.org/svn/murrine/trunk/ murrine
cd murrine
./autogen.sh --prefix=/usr --enable-animation
make
sudo make install
```

However, Cygoku on the Gnome-look.org website has also been posting .DEB packages for Ubuntu Intrepid. It has been updated everytime a new revision comes out: [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Murrine+Gtk2+Engine+DEB?content=96422](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Murrine+Gtk2+Engine+DEB?content=96422)

### Post by josedb on 2009-01-06
Ubuntu 8.10 32b
Turion 64 2.2ghz nVidia 7150 3gb ram 250gb HD

[[IMG]http://img70.imageshack.us/img70/792/pantallazoig5.th.png[/IMG]](http://img70.imageshack.us/my.php?image=pantallazoig5.png)

**Wallpaper**: from deviantart.com 7834_by_lassekorsgaard.jpg
**Icontheme**: JungleBlack
**fonts**: AlMateen Bold
**Controls**: Darker Theme
**Window decorations**: Elegant Brit
**Pointer**: DMZ white


**Conky**:

```
background no
font Sans:size=7
xftfont Sans:size=7
#xftfont Andale Mono-9
#xftfont Clean-8
#xftfont cubicfive10:pixelsize=8
#xftfont squaredance10:pixelsize=14
#xftfont swf!t_v02:pixelsize=10
use_xft yes
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1
#total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
minimum_size 300 5
maximum_width 280
default_color white #black #d7d7d7
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color red #black
alignment top_right
gap_x 2
gap_y 10
no_buffers yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
use_spacer no
override_utf8_locale yes
net_avg_samples 2
color0 cyan
color1 lightblue
color2 orange
color3 yellow
color4 wheat
color5 white
color6 white
color7 white
color8 white
color9 white
text_buffer_size 6000
TEXT
${voffset 6}${font arial black:size=30}${color2}${time %e}$color $font ${voffset 
-17}${time %A, }${time %B} ${time %G}
${voffset -2}${goto 65}${font arial black:size=15} ${time %I:%M:%S %p} $font
Uptime:$uptime

$color4 Batt:$color ${battery} $alignc ${color #E1D93F}${battery_bar 8} $color

${color1}SYSTEM $color ${hr 1 }
Hostname: $alignr$nodename
Kernel: $alignr$kernel
Processes: ${alignr}$processes ($running_processes running)
Load: ${alignr}$loadavg
CPU 1  ${execi 30 cat /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/scaling_governor}    ${alignc} ${freq}MHz / ${hwmon 0 temp 1 input}C ${alignr}(${cpu cpu1}%)
CPU 2  ${execi 30 cat /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/scaling_governor}    ${alignc} ${freq}MHz / ${hwmon 0 temp 3 input}C ${alignr}(${cpu cpu2}%)
${cpugraph}
${color1}RAM$color ${hr 1}

${alignr}$mem / $memmax ($memperc%)
${membar 4}
${color1}FILESYSTEM $color${hr 1}${color}

Root: ${fs_free_perc /}% ${alignr}${fs_free /} / ${fs_size /}
${fs_bar 4 /}

${color1}NETWORK $color ${hr 1}${color}
IP Addres: ${addr eth0} ${alignr}External:$font${execi 14400 wget -O - http://whatismyip.org/ | tail}
IP Addres: ${addr ath0}                 
                   
${color1}  ${alignc}       Ethernet   $color
Down ${color green}${downspeed eth0} $color k/s ${alignr}Up ${color red}${upspeed eth0} $color k/s
${downspeedgraph eth0 25,107} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 25,107}
Total ${totaldown eth0} ${alignr}Total ${totalup eth0}

                          ${color1} ${alignc} Wlan $color
Down ${color green}${downspeed ath0} $color k/s ${alignr}Up ${color red}${upspeed ath0}$color k/s
${downspeedgraph ath0 25,107} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph ath0 25,107}
Total ${totaldown ath0} ${alignr}Total ${totalup ath0}

${color1}METEOROLOGIA${color}${hr 1}

${alignc}${color1}Desde:$color Buenos Aires, Argentina

${color1}Lat: ${color2}34°35'S          ${alignc}${color1}Long: ${color2}58°21'W         ${alignr}${color1}Alt: ${color2}25 m$color
${voffset 5}${color2}${font Sans:size=10}Hoy:$font ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=CC}$color${alignr 2}${color1}ST: ${color2}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=LT}
${color3}${font Weather:size=50}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=WF}$font$color
${alignr 50}${voffset -55}${font Sans:size=25}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=HT}$font
${alignc 20}${voffset -30}${font Arrows:size=20}${color4}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=BF}$color$font
${alignc 10}${voffset 5}${color4}Viento: ${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=WS}$color
${color1}Humedad: ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=HM}${alignr 2}${color1}Precipitación: ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=PC}$color
${alignc}${color1}Presión: ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=BR} - ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=BD}$color

${color1}Salida del Sol: ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=SR}${alignr 2}${color1}Ocaso: ${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=SS}$color
${voffset 15}${color1}Luna:${color4}${alignr 2}${color3}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=MP}$color
${voffset -20}${offset 80}${color4}${font moon phases:size=20}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=ARBA0009 --datatype=MF}$font$color

```

### Post by Piraja on 2009-01-10
A series of screenshots to show how I'm using transparency and exploiting ideas from many individuals on this forum and some others &#8212; I must mention Eightmillion (I picked the idea of transparent backgrounds from one of his posts, and Lyricsdownloader is indeed his masterwork) and Bruce M who showed me how to launch several conkies by one click. The background image is one I gimped from a *Yukon Raven* photo by [Gavatron]("http://search.creativecommons.org/?q=yukon+raven&sourceid=Mozilla-search#") (Creative Commons). For the borderless Gnome Terminal I followed instructions by [Beowulf]("http://linux.derkeiler.com/Newsgroups/alt.os.linux/2006-11/msg00232.html") &#8212; his AllTray solution does not work perfectly with the present GNOME panel, however, and I might try something different instead.*****

[[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00820/3353507.t.png[/img]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3353507.png) [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00035/3353485.t.png[/img]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3353485.png) [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00062/3353478.t.png[/img]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3353478.png) [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00102/3353475.t.png[/img]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3353475.png)

*** (later edits)** I tried to make the Gnome terminal undecorated taking heed of various suggestions, including Devil's Pie, but none of these had satisfactory consequences. Too much ado. [**Tilda**]("http://www.linuxhaxor.net/2008/05/01/configuring-linux-terminal-to-work-as-a-transparent-wallpaper-part-1/#comment-15338")'s all I really need. Such a smart young lass.

In case you want to view and/or download the background image, please right-click on the thumbnail below and open it in a new tab or window. Left-clicking produces just a black pop-up window, because the forum popup-thingy cannot handle transparency.

---

Ok, here's mine.

[http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/Screenshot-4.png](http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/Screenshot-4.png)

[http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/Screenshot-5.png](http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/Screenshot-5.png)

Wallpaper: [http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/11588-1024x768-blue-eyes.jpg](http://i240.photobucket.com/albums/ff15/laurielegit/11588-1024x768-blue-eyes.jpg)
Icons: [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=72619&vote=good&tan=94004017](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=72619&vote=good&tan=94004017)
Controls: Xfce-dusk
Window Border: Tenebrific
Conky: Using ConkyPidgin and ConkyEmail scripts, here is my conkyRC:
```

# Conky configuration
background no
use_xft yes
xftfont sans:size=9
xftalpha 0.8
out_to_console no
update_interval 1
total_run_times 0
own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes
stippled_borders 5
border_margin 4
border_width 1
default_color grey
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black
alignment top_right
gap_x 10
gap_y 40
no_buffers no
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer yes
alignment top_left
text_buffer_size 2048

TEXT
${color white}${alignc}$nodename - $kernel - Uptime: $uptime 
$color$stippled_hr
${color white}${alignc}Network: Wireless
${color grey}${alignc}${addr wlan0}
${color white}Bandwidth: ${color grey}       Up: ${color grey}${upspeed wlan0} k/s     ${color grey}Down: ${color grey}${downspeed wlan0} k/s	    
                         ${color grey}${totalup wlan0} Up      ${color grey}${totaldown wlan0} Down
$color$stippled_hr
${color white}${alignc}Unread Emails:
${alignc}${execi 1800 conkyEmail -t /home/laurie/Source/.conkyemail}$color$stippled_hr
${color white}${alignc}Load Average - ${loadavg}
${color grey}${alignc}Processes: ${color grey} $processes  ${color grey}Running:${color grey} $running_processes
${color white}Name:                    ${alignr}PID     CPU%   MEM%
  ${color grey} ${top name 1}     ${alignr}${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1} ${top mem 1}
  ${color grey} ${top name 2}     ${alignr}${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2} ${top mem 2}
  ${color grey} ${top name 3}     ${alignr}${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3} ${top mem 3}
  ${color grey} ${top name 4}     ${alignr}${top pid 4} ${top cpu 4} ${top mem 4}
${color white}Memory Usage:
  ${color grey} ${top_mem name 1} ${alignr}${top_mem pid 1} ${top_mem cpu 1} ${top_mem mem 1}
  ${color grey} ${top_mem name 2} ${alignr}${top_mem pid 2} ${top_mem cpu 2} ${top_mem mem 2}
  ${color grey} ${top_mem name 3} ${alignr}${top_mem pid 3} ${top_mem cpu 3} ${top_mem mem 3}
  ${color grey} ${top_mem name 4} ${alignr}${top_mem pid 4} ${top_mem cpu 4} ${top_mem mem 4}
$color$stippled_hr
${color white}CPU: $color ${color grey}${color white}     Usage: ${color grey} ${cpu}% ${color white}${cpubar}
                           RAM: $memperc% ${membar}
                         SWAP:  $swapperc% ${swapbar}
$color$stippled_hr
${color white}${alignc}Drives
${color white}System: ${alignc}${color grey}${fs_used /}${color white}/${color grey}${fs_size /} ${color white}${alignr}(${color grey}${fs_free /} ${fs_free_perc /}% ${color white} free)
         ${fs_bar /}
${color white}Home Directory: ${alignc}${color grey}${fs_used /home}${color white}/${color grey}${fs_size /home} ${color white}${alignr}(${color grey}${fs_free /home} ${fs_free_perc /home}% ${color white} free)
         ${fs_bar /home}
${color white}External: ${alignc}${color grey}${fs_used /media/disk}${color white}/${color grey}${fs_size /media/disk} ${color white}${alignr}(${color grey}${fs_free /media/disk} ${fs_free_perc /media/disk}% ${color white} free)
         ${fs_bar /media/disk}
$color$stippled_hr
${alignc}${color white}Pidgin:
${alignc}${execpi 60 conkyPidgin -o --ignorelist="No Conky" --limit 6 -C Available -t /usr/share/conkypidgin/example/conkyPidgin.template --sortbylogactivity}
$color$stippled_hr
```

I've got *lots* of transparency, and i love it. I did have a dock, but got so fed up with it that I reinstated my gnome-panel and made it transparent (using compiz).

### Post by mishathegoat on 2009-01-10
> **dbbolton said:**
> Awesome. Mind posting your tintrc?

Thanks for the compliment! The effect I achieved was accomplished by editing my wallpaper so that both my tint and cairo-dock had the same "background". I set my desktop margins so that my windows would not overlap them. I'm sure my tintrc would not look the same as they would without the edited wallpaper. But here it is anywho..

tintrc
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_monitor
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = top center
panel_size = 1220 28
panel_margin = 0 20
panel_padding = 0 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 0
panel_border_width = 0
panel_background_color = #000000 0
panel_border_color = #ffffff 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 120
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 6
task_icon_size = 13
task_font = sans 7
task_font_color = #ffffff 70
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 85

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 0
task_background_color = #ffffff 0
task_active_background_color = #ffffff 50
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 18

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = sans 8
#time2_format = %A %d %B
#time2_font = sans 6
clock_font_color = #ffffff 76

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

### Post by Piraja on 2009-01-10
> **boost3d23 said:**
> BTW does anyone know how to get the area around the windows transparent (ex. notice the terminal)?
You mean the window borders (or controls?), like this:

[[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00708/3358468.t.png[/IMG]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3358468.png)

I just began experimenting with **transset**. A neat little treat.

*P.S.* To be more explicit: sudo apt-get install transset. In the terminal, type transset. You'll see what happens, it's really easy to play around with it. I don't know yet so much about it, just gave it a try.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-01-11
> **urukrama said:**
> Assuming that text editor is vim, could you post your configuration files for it? The colours look very pretty. :-)

Thats just the standard tango color scheme mate. Here is it neway.

tango.vim

```
"
" Tango Vim Color Scheme
" =======================
"
" For best results, set up your terminal with a Tango palette.
" Instructions for GNOME Terminal:
" http://uwstopia.nl/blog/2006/07/tango-terminal
"
" author:   Michele Campeotto <micampe@micampe.it>
"
set background=dark

hi clear
if exists("syntax_on")
    syntax reset
endif

let colors_name = "tango"

" Default Colors
hi Normal       guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#000000
hi NonText      guifg=#555753 guibg=#000000 gui=none
hi NonText      ctermfg=darkgray
hi Cursor       guibg=#d3d7cf
hi lCursor      guibg=#d3d7cf

" Search
hi Search       guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#c4a000
hi Search       cterm=none ctermfg=grey ctermbg=blue
hi IncSearch    guibg=#eeeeec guifg=#729fcf
hi IncSearch    cterm=none ctermfg=yellow ctermbg=green

" Window Elements
hi StatusLine   guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#4e9a06 gui=bold
hi StatusLine   ctermfg=white ctermbg=green cterm=bold
hi StatusLineNC guifg=#d3d7df guibg=#4e9a06
hi StatusLineNC ctermfg=lightgray ctermbg=darkgreen
hi VertSplit    guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#eeeeec
hi Folded       guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#75507b
hi Folded       ctermfg=white ctermbg=magenta
hi Visual       guifg=#d3d7cf guibg=#4e9a06
hi Visual       ctermbg=white ctermfg=lightgreen cterm=reverse

" Specials
hi Todo         guifg=#8ae234 guibg=#4e9a06 gui=bold
hi Todo         ctermfg=white ctermbg=green
hi Title        guifg=#eeeeec gui=bold
hi Title        ctermfg=white cterm=bold

" Syntax
hi Constant     guifg=#c4a000
hi Constant     ctermfg=darkyellow
hi Number       guifg=#729fcf
hi Number       ctermfg=darkblue
hi Statement    guifg=#4e9a06 gui=bold
hi Statement    ctermfg=green
" hi Identifier   guifg=#8ae234
" hi Identifier   ctermfg=darkgreen
hi Identifier   guifg=#8866cc
hi Identifier   ctermfg=darkblue
hi PreProc      guifg=#cc0000
hi PreProc      ctermfg=darkred
hi Comment      guifg=#06989a gui=italic
hi Comment      ctermfg=cyan cterm=none
hi Type         guifg=#d3d7cf gui=bold
hi Type         ctermfg=gray cterm=bold
hi Special      guifg=#75507b
hi Special      ctermfg=magenta cterm=none
hi Error        guifg=#eeeeec guibg=#ef2929
hi Error        ctermfg=white ctermbg=red

" Diff
hi DiffAdd      guifg=fg guibg=#3465a4 gui=none
hi DiffAdd      ctermfg=gray ctermbg=blue cterm=none
hi DiffChange   guifg=fg guibg=#555753 gui=none
hi DiffChange   ctermfg=gray ctermbg=darkgray cterm=none
hi DiffDelete   guibg=bg
hi DiffDelete   ctermfg=gray ctermbg=none cterm=none
hi DiffText     guifg=fg guibg=#c4a000 gui=none
hi DiffText     ctermfg=gray ctermbg=yellow cterm=none

```

here's my .vimrc

```
set nocompatible

" allow backspacing over everything in insert mode
set backspace=indent,eol,start

" enable code folding
set foldenable
set foldmethod=indent
set foldlevel=100
set foldopen-=search
set foldopen-=undo

set paste
set smartindent
set nobackup
set number
set nowrap
set nobackup
set history=10
set ruler
set showcmd
set incsearch
set hlsearch
set tabstop=2
set shiftwidth=2
set tabstop=2

syntax on

colorscheme tango

```

### Post by foo_bar on 2009-01-12
> **sujoy said:**
> nice :)
how did you get that terminal with transparent background? when i set alpha from the titlebar it also makes the text transparent, i have xcompmgr running too, but somehow, its not working :confused:

I installed aterm and run this string in the fluxbox startup config file: 

```
aterm -name aterm -sl 3000 -tr +sb -si -sk -sh 0 -fb -schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-*-120-*-*-c-*-iso8859-1 -g 200x400-3+0 -bl -fg \#FEFEFE &
```

I created an .Xdefaults file in my home directory with this in it:

```
Aterm*geometry: 200x800
Aterm*foreground: #FEFEFE
Aterm*transparent: true
Aterm*shading: 0
Aterm*font: schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-*-120-*-*-c-*-iso8859-1
Aterm*saveLines: 3000
Aterm*borderLess: true
Aterm*scrollBar: false
Aterm*iconName: aterm
```

and finally added this in the fluxbox apps config file:

```
[app] (name=aterm)
  [Dimensions]	{516 781}
  [Position]	(UPPERLEFT)	{0 0}
  [Hidden]	{yes}
  [Sticky]	{yes}
  [Layer]	{12}
[end]
```


I realize there's quite a bit of redundancy there but I haven't figured out which, if any, of the configs files I can chop down and still have it work. I tried a bit of trial and error, but well.. not enough yet. I'll get it tommorrow.

---

### Post by uberdonkey5 on 2009-01-12
> **sujoy said:**
> nice :)
how did you get that terminal with transparent background? when i set alpha from the titlebar it also makes the text transparent, i have xcompmgr running too, but somehow, its not working :confused:

A much easier method and I believe much prettier, is to install Tilda. For example I have produced a tiny terminal with some transparency and green background. Tilda allows you to pop up the terminal from the corner with a single key (usually an 'F' key, though I use the menu key). You can size it, position it (anywhere) and colour it as you want.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-01-12
> **Piraja said:**
> Hmm... Maybe I'm not getting something, but have you considered installing one of Firefox's add-on themes? They are not overridden by Gnome (or whatever) themes. I have been using Dark Revisited on another machine (not in the screenshot, which portrays just the FF Addon Page).

What I mean is, I want Firefox to use the GTK theme, but textboxes in pages NOT to. What happens is a dark GTK theme affects textboxes and they end up with black backgrounds and occasionally white text (often times black or dark text, requiring a fix). I'd like it if FF would just keep normal textboxes.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-01-13
> **Nythain said:**
> whats even more beautiful is thats xfce, an environment i've never really seen look so good :)

Don't think it really qualifies as an Xfce desktop. He replaced xfce4-panel with tint2, xfwm4 with compiz + emerald and none of the running applications are Xfce applications. It's basically just xfdesktop and presumably the xfce-mcs-manager.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-01-13
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Don't think it really qualifies as an Xfce desktop. He replaced xfce4-panel with tint2, xfwm4 with compiz + emerald and none of the running applications are Xfce applications. It's basically just xfdesktop and presumably the xfce-mcs-manager.

That really does leave us with the question of what makes a desktop whatever DE it is. Considering you could have an XFCE and a GNOME user both running Compiz/Emerald with Tint2 or AWN, what separates them? Default filemanager? Heck you can run Compiz as its own WM and then throw Tint on it. You don't need XFCE -or- GNOME for it.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-01-13
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> That really does leave us with the question of what makes a desktop whatever DE it is. Considering you could have an XFCE and a GNOME user both running Compiz/Emerald with Tint2 or AWN, what separates them? Default filemanager? Heck you can run Compiz as its own WM and then throw Tint on it. You don't need XFCE -or- GNOME for it.

I don't want to get into a philosophical discussion over the taxonomy of DMs, it's simply incorrect to lump one thing in with a bunch of others when there are fundamental differences present in such gross proportions.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-01-14
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> I don't want to get into a philosophical discussion over the taxonomy of DMs, it's simply incorrect to lump one thing in with a bunch of others when there are fundamental differences present in such gross proportions.

My point is what's different from the end user perspective. If I'm using Firefox to browse, Pidgin to chat, PCManFM for filemanager, Sonata/MPD for music, Tint2 is my panel, Compiz/Emerald are taking care of my windows... is there any difference to me between the various DE's that allow that setup? Heck I'm on OB right now and these are the only differences between it and GNOME from the end-user standpoint:

- Can't put icons on the desktop
- Right-click menu
- No effects (which means a panel instead of AWN)
- Openbox themes instead of Metacity themes

There. Nothing else has really changed for me. I don't use a single different application, my usage hasn't altered in the slightest. I'm sure there are lots of under the hood differences, but if they don't manifest into a different experience for the user, what's the point?

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-01-14
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> My point is what's different from the end user perspective. If I'm using Firefox to browse, Pidgin to chat, PCManFM for filemanager, Sonata/MPD for music, Tint2 is my panel, Compiz/Emerald are taking care of my windows... is there any difference to me between the various DE's that allow that setup? Heck I'm on OB right now and these are the only differences between it and GNOME from the end-user standpoint:

- Can't put icons on the desktop
- Right-click menu
- No effects (which means a panel instead of AWN)
- Openbox themes instead of Metacity themes

There. Nothing else has really changed for me. I don't use a single different application, my usage hasn't altered in the slightest. I'm sure there are lots of under the hood differences, but if they don't manifest into a different experience for the user, what's the point?

This really diverges from our original issue:> whats even more beautiful is thats xfce, an environment i've never really seen look so good
If Xfce can be defined so loosely, this statement is meaningless (why compare it only to other xfce shots if all distinctions are moot, as you've suggested?). If Xfce is strictly defined as all stock apps and components, we're again left with a meaningless statement since the shot he's referring to doesn't fit that profile.

My objection was simple; if we can be so liberal in our distinctions, we should not then be so finite in our comparisons.

### Post by ghindo on 2009-01-15

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2009-01-15
> **ghindo said:**
> I'm actually using Arch, like you :p
Well then here it is, lol.
```

#!/usr/bin/perl
use Switch;

use strict;

####################
## Config options ##
####################

## What distro logo to use to use, Available "Archlinux Debian None" ##
my $distro = "Archlinux";

## what values to display. Use "OS Kernel DE WM win_theme Theme Font Icons" ##
my $display = "OS Kernel DE WM Win_theme Wallpaper Theme Icons Font CPU";

## Takes a screen shot if set to 0 ##
my $shot = 0;
## Command to run to take screen shot ##
my $command = "scrot '%m.%d.%Y-shot.png' -d 5";

## What colors to use for the variables. ##
my $textcolor = "\e[0m";

## Prints little debugging messages if set to 0 ##
my $quite = 0;

########################
## Script starts here ##
########################
## Define some thing to work with strict ##
my @line = ();
my $found = 0;
my $DE = "NONE";
my $WM = "NONE";

## Hash of WMs and the process they run ##
my %WMlist = ("Beryl", "beryl",
          "Compiz", "compiz",
              "Fluxbox", "fluxbox",
              "Openbox", "openbox",
              "Blackbox", "blackbox",
              "Xfwm4", "xfwm4",
              "Metacity", "metacity",
              "Kwin", "kwin",
              "FVWM", "fvwm",
              "Enlightenment", "enlightenment",
              "IceWM", "icewm",
              "Window Maker", "wmaker",
          "AwesomeWM", "awesomewm",
              "PekWM","pekwm" );

## Hash of DEs and the process they run ##     
my %DElist = ("Gnome", "gnome-session",
              "Xfce4", "xfce-mcs-manage",
              "KDE", "ksmserver");

## Get Kernel version ##
if ( $display =~ "Kernel"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Kernel version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $kernel = `uname -r`;
  $kernel =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $kernel = " Kernel:$textcolor $kernel";
  push(@line, "$kernel");
}


## Get CPU ##
#if ( $display =~ "CPU"){
#  print "\::$textcolor Finding Processor\n" unless $quite == 1;
#  my $CPU = `(grep "model name" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2 | head -n1| sed  -r "s/\s+/ /g")`;
#  $CPU = " CPU:$textcolor $CPU";
#  push(@line, "$CPU");
#}

## Find running processes ##
print "\::$textcolor Getting processes \n" unless $quite == 1;
my $processes = `ps -A | awk {'print \$4'}`;

## Find DE ##
while( (my $DEname, my $DEprocess) = each(%DElist) ) {
  print "\::$textcolor Testing $DEname process: $DEprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$DEprocess/ ) {
    $DE = $DEname;
    print "\::$textcolor DE found as $DE\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/DE/ ) {
      push(@line, " DE:$textcolor $DE");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM ##
while( (my $WMname, my $WMprocess) = each(%WMlist) ) {
 print "\::$textcolor Testing $WMname process: $WMprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$WMprocess/ ) {
    $WM = $WMname;
    print "\::$textcolor WM found as $WM\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/WM/ ) {
      push(@line, " WM:$textcolor $WM");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM theme ##
if ( $display =~ m/Win_theme/ ){
  switch($WM) {
    case "Openbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/openbox/rc.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<name>(.+)<\/name>/ ) {
          while ( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Compiz" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.emerald/theme/theme.ini")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /name=(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Metacity" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /apps/metacity/general/theme`;
      print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $gconf\n" unless $quite == 1;
      chomp ($gconf);
      push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
    }
    case "Fluxbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.fluxbox/init")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Blackbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.blackboxrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Xfwm4" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/xfwm4.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<option name="Xfwm\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
  } 
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Kwin" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kwinrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /PluginLib=kwin3_(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Enlightenment" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $remote = `enlightenment_remote -theme-get theme` ;
      if( $remote =~ m/.*FILE="(.+).edj"/ ) {
        print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
      }     
    }       
    case "IceWM" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.icewm/theme")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme="(.+)\/.*.theme/ ) {
          while( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }   
      close(FILE);
    }   
    case "PekWM" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.pekwm/config")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme.*\/(.*)"/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE); 
    } 
  }   
}     
      
## Find Theme Icon ans Font ##
if ( $display =~ m/[Theme, Icons, Font, Wallpaper]/) {
  switch($DE) {
    case "Gnome" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
      if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $gconf");
      } 
      if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
    } 
    case "Xfce4" {
      my @sort = ();
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/gtk.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
     if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/IconThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="Gtk\/FontName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Font:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
      ## Sort variables so they're ordered "Theme Icon Font" ##
      foreach my $i (@sort) {
        push(@line, "$i");
      }
open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/desktop.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if ( $display =~ m/Wallpaper/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="imagepath_0_0" type="string" value=".*\/(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\:: Wallpaper found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wallpaper:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    } 
    case "KDE" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kdeglobals")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) { 
        if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if ( /widgetStyle=(.+)/  ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Wiget Style found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wiget Style:$textcolor $1");
          }
          if (/colorScheme=(.+).kcsrc/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Color Scheme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Color Scheme:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if ( /Theme=(.+)/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }   
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /font=(.+)/ ) {
            my $font = (split/,/, $1)[0];
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $font\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $font");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    else {
      my @files = ("$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc-2.0", "$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc.mine",);
      foreach my $file (@files) {
        if ( -e $file ) {
          print "\::$textcolor Opening $file\n" unless $quite == 1; 
          open(FILE, $file)
          || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
          while( <FILE> ) {
            if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
              if( /include ".*themes\/(.+)\/gtk-(1|2)\.0\/gtkrc"/ ){
                print "\::$textcolor GTK theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-icon-theme-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-font-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $1");
             }
            }
          }
          close(FILE);
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

## Display the system info ##
if ( $distro =~ m/Archlinux/ ) {

## Get Archlinux version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Archlinux version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/arch-release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}

my $c1 = "\e[1;32m";
my $c2 = "\e[0;32m";
my $c3 = "\e[0;32m";
print "$c2
$c2
$c2
$c2                       __      $c1 ___                                 
$c2                      /\\ \\    $c1 /\\_ \\    __                          
$c2     __     _ __   ___\\ \\ \\___ $c1\\//\\ \\  /\\_\\    ___   __  __  __  _  
$c2   /'__`\\  /\\`'__\\/'___\\ \\  _ `\\ $c1\\ \\ \\ \\/\\ \\ /' _ `\\/\\ \\/\\ \\/\\ \\/'\\ 
$c2  /\\ \\L\\.\\_\\ \\ \\//\\ \\__/\\ \\ \\ \\ \\ $c1\\_\\ \\_\\ \\ \\/\\ \\/\\ \\ \\ \\_\\ \\/>  </ 
$c2  \\ \\__/.\\_\\\\ \\_\\\\ \\____\\\\ \\_\\ \\_\\$c1/\\____\\\\ \\_\\ \\_\\ \\_\\ \\____//\\_/\\_\\
$c2   \\/__/\\/_/ \\/_/ \\/____/ \\/_/\\/_/$c1\\/____/ \\/_/\\/_/\\/_/\\/___/ \\//\\/_/
$c1   
$c1      $c3@line[0]
$c1      $c3@line[1]
$c1      $c3@line[2]
$c1      $c3@line[3]
$c1      $c3@line[4]
$c1      $c3@line[5]
$c1      $c3@line[6]
$c1      $c3@line[7]
$c1      $c3@line[8]
$c2
$c2
\e[0m";
}


if ( $distro =~ m/None/ ) {
my $color = "\e[0;31m";
  foreach my $filled ( @line ) {
    print "$color $filled\n"
  }
}

if ( $distro =~ m/Debian/ ) {

## Get Debian version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Debian version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/Debian_release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}
my $c1 = "\e[0;31m";

print "
$c1       _,met\$\$\$\$\$gg.
$c1    ,g\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$P.
$c1  ,g\$\$P\"\"       \"\"\"Y\$\$.\".              @line[0]
$c1 ,\$\$P'              \`\$\$\$.              @line[1]
$c1',\$\$P       ,ggs.     \`\$\$b:            @line[2]
$c1\`d\$\$'     ,\$P\"'   .    \$\$\$             @line[3]
$c1 \$\$P      d\$'     ,    \$\$P             @line[4]
$c1 \$\$:      \$\$.   -    ,d\$\$'             @line[5]
$c1 \$\$\;      Y\$b._   _,d\$P'               @line[6]
$c1 Y\$\$.    \`.\`\"Y\$\$\$\$P\"'                  @line[7]
$c1 \`\$\$b      \"-.__                       @line[8]
$c1  \`Y\$\$
$c1   \`Y\$\$.
$c1     \`\$\$b.
$c1       \`Y\$\$b.
$c1          \`\"Y\$b._
$c1              \`\"\"\"\"
\e[0m";   
}       

     
## Run screen shot graper ##
`$command` unless $shot != 0;

```

${goto 20}${rss http://www.sbs.com.au/news/rss/Section/Top%20Stories 10 item_title 4}${goto 210}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 220}${rss http://www.sbs.com.au/news/rss/Section/National 10 item_title 4}${goto 410}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 420}${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/world/rss.xml 10 item_title 4}${goto 610}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 620}${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/idx-australia/rss.xml 10 item_title 4}${goto 810}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 820}${rss http://newsrss.bbc.co.uk/rss/newsonline_world_edition/front_page/rss.xml 10 item_title 4}${goto 1010}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 1020}${rss http://feeds.news.com.au/public/rss/2.0/anow_state_191.xml 10 item_title 4}${goto 1210}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${goto 1220}${rss http://rss.slashdot.org/Slashdot/slashdot 10 item_title 4}${goto 1420}${color4}${outlinecolor 101010}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${outlinecolor 252525}${voffset 4}${goto 0}${outlinecolor 151515}${color3}______________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
${goto 1000}__________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________________
```

(the underscore abuse at the bottom was my attempt to shave a couple of pixels off the vertical size.)

Okay, when writing your own (or modifying mine), take note that:

- the easier way of doing RSS in conky (using the item_titles <number of titles> argument) refuses to let you use a horizontal layout. Trying to put anything left or right of the rss feed - including more feeds - results in only the first headline being correctly formatted, with everything on proceeding lines ending up jumbled on the left of your screen.

This is why I use the item_title (note the singular *title*, not plural *titles* argument and why there's 5 times as much ...markup (?).

Eg. the basic format goes as follows:
```
${rss <first feed url> item_title 0} ${rss <second feed url> item_title 0}
${rss <first feed url> item_title 1} ${rss <second feed url> item_title 1}
```

- I've heavily abused both ${goto} and ${fsbar} to get feeds closer together without having overlapping text. Well, the text still overlaps, you just can't see it because the ${fsbar}s are the same colour as conky's window's background. Also note that in order to get ${fsbar}s to appear full, you just need to direct it to a non-existent folder (hence all the /fakelol/ bits in my conkyrc.

- If you're going to use my dirty method of getting feeds closer together, I suggest you change draw_outlines and draw_shades to *no* to avoid having funky borders on the ${fsbar} which are *supposed* to be invisible. You can keep shades and outlines if you want to but it requires a much more complicated file to get around the fsbar borders (requiring you to manually change the outline/shade colour to your background colour before every fsbar and restoring the outline/shade colour to it's original colour after every fsbar).

- If you want a fully transparent conky, don't abuse fsbars. Otherwise, you get this (which also demonstrates what I've done quite succinctly):

[img]http://img398.imageshack.us/img398/615/conkyrssyf7.jpg[/img]

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-01-15
> **Piraja said:**
> Thanks for the tips: It's the same with the Gnome terminal, Xterm and with gmrun, too. 

I have also tried changing the Conky window type between normal, override and desktop, but I can reproduce the jigsaw puzzle in spite of those changes.

did you try the kill command as well? Find the process id of your conky first and send the kill command.

i think this will give your PID on your terminal

```
ps -gx
```

Once you know your conky PID then use kill command

```
kill PID
```

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-01-16
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Yeah, I figured you'd either understand it; not understand it and perhaps shy away from conky for another year (like I did) or not understand it but after a couple of days of playing around with conky you'd read it and go, "oh yeah...".

Ahhkay, what's slim like, anyway? Is it easy to switch DE/WMs or is it like using login; you've got to keep editing your xinitrc file?
It's about as easy to use as GDM. If memory serves, it also picks up the .desktop entries in /usr/share/xsessions . The only difference is that you have to press Alt+F1 rather than clicking "Session" :D

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-01-17
That devART theme, while nice, was really starting to become an eyesore.  So I decided to go back and develop my black theme some more.

I found the wallpaper [here]("http://stlphx.deviantart.com/art/Headphones-109656004").  I was searching through the widescreen wallpapers and this one struck my eye for some reason.  I don't normally use non-abstract wallpapers, but I really like this one.

The Emerald theme is basically a modification of the [Dots Emerald]("http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/Dots-Emerald-100238296").  I modified it to use the vrunner engine instead of the pixmap engine, so that I could color it to match my windows.

### Post by jomiolto on 2009-01-17
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Honestly, building and installing qgtkstyle really is a piece of piss. I don't get why so many people are reluctant to try it.

I don't understand how that would solve the problems with my dislike for dark themes in VLC ;)

I'm just so used to VLC being light gray, that anything else just feels wrong, no matter how it's done and how much it doesn't fit in with a dark background/decorations of my desktop (I have the same problem with Firefox and OpenOffice too -- light text on dark background just seems "wrong" in them)...

Also, qgtkstyle is even less relevant in this case, because I happen to be using Hardy at the moment and the old version of VLC that doesn't use Qt :) Most of my time is spent on terminal, and VLC, Firefox and OpenOffice are actually the only "graphical" applications I spent a lot of time with, so I'm actually using a rather light GTK theme, even if the rest of my desktop is dark.

Hopefully that clears it up :)

### Post by Piraja on 2009-01-17

That's MOC, Music On Console, a gapless CLI player, VERY cool (nice themes too).

**EDIT**: Added the screenshot below. Unlike a few other themes that come with MOC, the Moca theme is not transparent by default, but I used transset to make it that. This is all the eye candy I want from a music player (well, I have to admit that Exaile's desktop cover plugin is nice, too).

### Post by spcwingo on 2009-01-18
My first cli build-up finished this morning.:biggrin:  This machine was doomed for the landfill before it caught my eye.  It's a P3 @ 800 Mhz w/256 MB RAM.  The only thing that was wrong with it was a bad PCI riser card.  A quick stop by ebay and $6 later it's up and running.  The total install size is 875.36 MB.  Well, enough of that here's the screenie.

[screenshot]("http://i91.photobucket.com/albums/k306/spcwingo/screenshot-1.png")

I know it's still a bit plain, but I'm working on it.;)

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-01-18
> **tr4nce said:**
> Nothing fancy

[[img]http://omploader.org/tMTU4MQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMTU4MQ)That's pretty good. Your GTK+ theme could do with a little more finesse but simplicity really does work a treat.

> **danielrmt said:**
> Great screenie. How can do you get that nice feed reader in the desktop?

> **ddnev45 said:**
> It's part of his conky setup:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6551579#post6551579]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6551579#post6551579")

I realised the fsbar abuse left most of the text without outlines anyway so here's a somewhat cleaner, simpler config:

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Lucida Grande:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color ffffff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 252525
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 afafaf #bfbfbf #cfcfcf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 111111 #1a1a1a #720000
color4 0a0a0a #101010

own_window yes
own_window_colour 0a0a0a
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x -3
gap_y 20 #14
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT

### Post by piepants on 2009-01-19
Slowly been refining my eye candy!

Got the idea for the "taskbar" from an earlier post in this thread - it's drawn on the wallpaper, with Conky handling the time & Rhythmbox info, Avant for the dock, and just a non-expanded Gnome bar for the system tray.

Theme: BiMetallico
Icons: Gion
Fonts: Mostly Segoe UI, Cambria for the clock (both Vista fonts), with DejaVu Sans Mono Book for the console.

### Post by piepants on 2009-01-19
> **amitabhishek said:**
> ^^How did you make your Firefox translucent?

It's the trail focus option in Compiz

If you have the CompizConfig settings manager installed, it's under Effects -> Trailfocus

### Post by blazemore on 2009-01-19
I personally think this should be used as the default theme at some point. It's so classy.

Wallpaper: Can't remember but I'll upload if people want (If you find it PM me and I'll put the link here)

GTK: Shiki Colors

Metacity: Shiki Colors

I replaced the "Selected Items" with brown, and the "window colour" with the background colour from acne.org to create the subtle feel, rather than Shiki Human's default garish orange.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-01-20
> **ayoli said:**
> Could you share your exaile layout, please ?They've not made it as easy anymore, with the considerable rewrite they've done. It's not as simple as just putting a glade file in your $HOME/.exaile folder.

You're going to need to either download the 0.3a1 tarball or the latest weekly tarball (0.3a1 collection panel is broken so perhaps try the latest weekly): 
[http://www.exaile.org/](http://www.exaile.org/)

Then download my modded .glade and .py files:
[http://etnlicarus.googlepages.com/exaile_mod.tar.gz](http://etnlicarus.googlepages.com/exaile_mod.tar.gz) 

You don't need to build or install exaile, just extract the tarball to wherever you want. Then extract my tarball and put my files in their relative directories (eg ~/exaile_mod/data/glade/main.glade should go in ~/exaile/data/glade/, replacing the original main.glade).

Then run exaile.

Edit: Actually, I just tried the 7/1/09 and 14/1/09 weeklies and they're broken. Perhaps try an earlier build.

> Those from hydroxygen iconset aren't bad.Link?

---

### Post by ddnev45 on 2009-01-22
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Is NetBSD for netbooks or something?

I'm interested in trying out BSD, but I don't know which version to use.

No, it's a "regular" operating system. Plenty of documentation if you're looking to install it.

[http://www.netbsd.org/]("http://www.netbsd.org/")

I used both FreeBSD and NetBSD; each installed and ran just fine, but I didn't use either long enough to really give you a recommendation.

---

### Post by kk0sse54 on 2009-01-23
> **cardinals_fan said:**
> You're making me pine for NetBSD, and I don't even like KDE 4.  I'm sorely tempted to install it on my main box (I have it in a fairly major VM at the moment and on my old machine), despite issues with Flash and my wireless adapter.  If I can work up enough trust to count on my wireless connection staying up for more than ten minutes, I'm doing it.

I used to not like KDE4 back when I tested the nice and buggy 4.1 but it's finally starting to come together. I've pretty much given up on flash for the present time being and I've been lucky so far to have pretty good hardware compatibility. Otherwise damn that lack of various hardware support  in most BSDs...:)

> Is NetBSD for netbooks or something?

I'm interested in trying out BSD, but I don't know which version to use. 

Nah it's not for netbooks. If you've never used BSD you can check out some what of a brief comparison of the different ones [here.]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparison_of_BSD_operating_systems") Other wise if you want something user friendly check out PC-BSD or DesktopBSD or dive right in and test out one of the big three (FreeBSD, OpenBSD, NetBSD) by either installing on your hard disk or through vm.
